				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=McDonald%27s_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonald&#039;s Corp.">McDonald&#039;s Corp.</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<p class="mw-empty-elt">


</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Macdonald (disambiguation)">Macdonald (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"McD" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/MCD_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="MCD (disambiguation)">MCD (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"McDo" redirects here. For the Philippine subsidiary, see <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s_Philippines" title="McDonald's Philippines">McDonald's Philippines</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable plainlinks selfreference noprint selfref">For <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(technical_restrictions)#Forbidden_characters" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (technical restrictions)">technical reasons</a>, "McDonald's #1 Store Museum" redirects here. For the museum, see <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s_No._1_Store_Museum" title="McDonald's No. 1 Store Museum">McDonald's No. 1 Store Museum</a>.</div>
<p><b>McDonald's Corporation</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Fast_food" title="Fast food">fast food</a> company, founded in 1940 as a restaurant operated by <a href="/wiki/Richard_and_Maurice_McDonald" title="Richard and Maurice McDonald">Richard and Maurice McDonald</a>, in <a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino,_California" title="San Bernardino, California">San Bernardino, California</a>, United States. They rechristened their business as a <a href="/wiki/Hamburger" title="Hamburger">hamburger</a> stand, and later turned the company into a <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchise</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Arches" title="Golden Arches">Golden Arches logo</a> being introduced in 1953 at a location in <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>. In 1955, <a href="/wiki/Ray_Kroc" title="Ray Kroc">Ray Kroc</a>, a businessman, joined the company as a franchise agent and proceeded to purchase the chain from the McDonald brothers. McDonald's had its original headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Oak_Brook,_Illinois" title="Oak Brook, Illinois">Oak Brook, Illinois</a>, but moved its global headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> in June 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-west_side_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-west_side-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-move_HQ_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-move_HQ-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> US$32.811 billion</span> (2018)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">Total equity</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="nowrap"><img alt="Decrease" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Decrease" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> US$-6.258 billion</span> (2018)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">~ 210,000 (<span style="font-size:85%;">2018</span>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.mcdonalds.com/us/en-us.html">www.mcdonalds.com</a><br><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://corporate.mcdonalds.com">corporate<wbr></wbr>.mcdonalds<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><p>McDonald's is the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Restaurant_chain" class="mw-redirect" title="Restaurant chain">restaurant chain</a> by revenue,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> serving over 69 million customers daily in over 100 countries<sup id="cite_ref-ChicagoTribune60years_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChicagoTribune60years-10">[10]</a></sup> across 37,855 outlets as of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_10K_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_10K-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2016_10K_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_10K-12">[12]</a></sup> Although McDonald's is best known for its hamburgers, <a href="/wiki/Cheeseburger" title="Cheeseburger">cheeseburgers</a> and  <a href="/wiki/French_fries" title="French fries">french fries</a>, they feature chicken products, <a href="/wiki/Breakfast" title="Breakfast">breakfast</a> items, <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">soft drinks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milkshake" title="Milkshake">milkshakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wrap_(food)" title="Wrap (food)">wraps</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dessert" title="Dessert">desserts</a>. In response to changing consumer tastes and a negative backlash because of the unhealthiness of their food,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> the company has added to its menu <a href="/wiki/Salad" title="Salad">salads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fish_as_food" title="Fish as food">fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Smoothie" title="Smoothie">smoothies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fruit" title="Fruit">fruit</a>.  The McDonald's Corporation revenues come from the rent, royalties, and fees paid by the franchisees, as well as sales in company-operated restaurants. According to two reports published in 2018, McDonald's is the world's second-largest private employer with 1.7 million employees (behind <a href="/wiki/Walmart" title="Walmart">Walmart</a> with 2.3 million employees).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_McDonald%27s" title="History of McDonald's">History of McDonald's</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DowneyMcdonalds.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/DowneyMcdonalds.jpg/220px-DowneyMcdonalds.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/DowneyMcdonalds.jpg/220px-DowneyMcdonalds.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DowneyMcdonalds.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Oldest_McDonald%27s_restaurant" title="Oldest McDonald's restaurant">oldest operating McDonald's</a> restaurant is the third one built, opened in 1953. It is located at 10207 Lakewood Blvd. at Florence Ave. in <a href="/wiki/Downey,_California#Landmarks" title="Downey, California">Downey, California</a> (at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=McDonald%27s&amp;params=33.9471_N_118.1182_W_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">33°56′50″N</span> <span class="longitude">118°07′06″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">33.9471°N 118.1182°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">33.9471; -118.1182</span></span></span></a></span>)</div></div></div>
<p>Siblings <a href="/wiki/Richard_and_Maurice_McDonald" title="Richard and Maurice McDonald">Richard and Maurice McDonald</a> opened the first McDonald's at 1398 North E Street at West 14th Street in <a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino,_California" title="San Bernardino, California">San Bernardino, California</a> (at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=McDonald%27s&amp;params=34.1255_N_117.2946_W_"><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">34°07′32″N</span> <span class="longitude">117°17′41″W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">﻿ / ﻿</span><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">34.1255°N 117.2946°W</span><span style="display:none">﻿ / <span class="geo">34.1255; -117.2946</span></span></span></a></span>) on May 15, 1940, but it was not the McDonald's recognizable today; Ray Kroc made changes to the brothers' business to modernize it. The brothers introduced the "Speedee Service System" in 1948, putting into expanded use the principles of the modern <a href="/wiki/Fast_food#Overview" title="Fast food">fast-food restaurant</a> that their predecessor <a href="/wiki/White_Castle_(restaurant)" title="White Castle (restaurant)">White Castle</a> had put into practice more than two decades earlier.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The original mascot of McDonald's was a chef hat on top of a hamburger who was referred to as "Speedee". In 1962, the Golden Arches replaced Speedee as the universal mascot. The mascot, clown <a href="/wiki/Ronald_McDonald" title="Ronald McDonald">Ronald McDonald</a>, was introduced in 1965. He appeared in advertising to target their audience of children.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption-center{text-align:center;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:McDonald%27s_1940_logo.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/57/McDonald%27s_1940_logo.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="80" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="80"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 80px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/57/McDonald%27s_1940_logo.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="80"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Logo from 1940 until 1948</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:McDonald%27s_1948_logo.png" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/McDonald%27s_1948_logo.png/200px-McDonald%27s_1948_logo.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="96" data-file-width="317" data-file-height="152"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 96px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/McDonald%27s_1948_logo.png/200px-McDonald%27s_1948_logo.png" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="96"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Logo from 1948 until 1953</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:McDonald%27s_logo_(1953-1960).svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b2/McDonald%27s_logo_%281953-1960%29.svg/200px-McDonald%27s_logo_%281953-1960%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="35" data-file-width="379" data-file-height="67"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 200px;height: 35px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b2/McDonald%27s_logo_%281953-1960%29.svg/200px-McDonald%27s_logo_%281953-1960%29.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="200" data-height="35" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b2/McDonald%27s_logo_%281953-1960%29.svg/300px-McDonald%27s_logo_%281953-1960%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b2/McDonald%27s_logo_%281953-1960%29.svg/400px-McDonald%27s_logo_%281953-1960%29.svg.png 2x"> </span></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">Logo from 1953 until 1960</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>On May 4, 1961, McDonald's first filed for a U.S. <a href="/wiki/Trademark" title="Trademark">trademark</a> on the name "McDonald's" with the description "Drive-In Restaurant Services", which continues to be renewed. By September 13, McDonald's, under the guidance of Ray Kroc, filed for a trademark on a new logo—an overlapping, double-arched "M" symbol. But before the double arches, McDonald's used a single arch for the architecture of their buildings. Although the "<a href="/wiki/Golden_Arches" title="Golden Arches">Golden Arches</a>" logo appeared in various forms, the present version was not used until November 18, 1968, when the company was favored a U.S. trademark.
</p><p>The present corporation credits its founding to <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchised</a> businessman <a href="/wiki/Ray_Kroc" title="Ray Kroc">Ray Kroc</a> on April 15, 1955. This was in fact the ninth opened McDonald's restaurant overall, although this location was destroyed and rebuilt in 1984. Kroc purchased the McDonald brothers' equity in the company and began the company's worldwide reach.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (April 2020)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> Kroc was recorded as being an aggressive business partner, driving the McDonald brothers out of the industry.
</p><p>Kroc and the McDonald brothers fought for control of the business, as documented in Kroc's autobiography. The San Bernardino restaurant was eventually torn down in 1971, and the site was sold to the <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pollo" title="Juan Pollo">Juan Pollo</a> chain in 1976. This area serves as headquarters for the Juan Pollo chain, and a McDonald's and Route 66 museum.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> With the expansion of McDonald's into many international markets, the company has become a symbol of <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a> and the spread of the <a href="/wiki/American_way" title="American way">American way</a> of life. Its prominence has made it a frequent topic of public debates about <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Business_ethics" title="Business ethics">corporate ethics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Consumer" title="Consumer">consumer</a> <a href="/wiki/Moral_responsibility" title="Moral responsibility">responsibility</a>.
</p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_overview">Corporate overview</span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Facts_and_figures">Facts and figures</span></h3>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harlem_Micky_Dz.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Harlem_Micky_Dz.jpg/220px-Harlem_Micky_Dz.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2616" data-file-height="3488"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 293px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Harlem_Micky_Dz.jpg/220px-Harlem_Micky_Dz.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="293" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harlem_Micky_Dz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>By 1993, McDonald's had sold more than 100 billion hamburgers. The once widespread restaurant signs that boasted the number of sales, such as this one in <a href="/wiki/Harlem" title="Harlem">Harlem</a>, were left at "99 billion" because there was space for only two digits. This McDonald's closed in late 2019. <sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ronald_Reagan_-_McDonald%27s.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Ronald_Reagan_-_McDonald%27s.jpg/220px-Ronald_Reagan_-_McDonald%27s.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="482"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 106px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Ronald_Reagan_-_McDonald%27s.jpg/220px-Ronald_Reagan_-_McDonald%27s.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="106" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ronald_Reagan_-_McDonald%27s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The McDonald's in <a href="/wiki/Northport,_Alabama" title="Northport, Alabama">Northport, Alabama</a> commemorates U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan" title="Ronald Reagan">Ronald Reagan</a>'s visit</div></div></div>
<p>McDonald's restaurants are found in 120 countries and territories around the world and serve 68 million customers each day.<sup id="cite_ref-retrieved_October_10,_2013_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retrieved_October_10,_2013-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-daily_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-daily-20">[20]</a></sup> McDonald's operates 37,855 restaurants worldwide, employing more than 210,000 people as of the end of 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_10K_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_10K-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2016_10K_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_10K-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-retrieved_October_10,_2013_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-retrieved_October_10,_2013-19">[19]</a></sup> There are a total of 2,770 company-owned locations and 35,085 franchised locations, which includes 21,685 locations franchised to conventional franchisees, 7,225 locations licensed to developmental licensees, and 6,175 locations licensed to foreign affiliates.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_10K_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_10K-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2016_10K_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2016_10K-12">[12]</a></sup></p><p>Focusing on its core brand, McDonald's began <a href="/wiki/Divestment" title="Divestment">divesting</a> itself of other chains it had acquired during the 1990s. The company owned a majority stake in <a href="/wiki/Chipotle_Mexican_Grill" title="Chipotle Mexican Grill">Chipotle Mexican Grill</a> until October 2006, when McDonald's fully divested from Chipotle through a stock exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mcds-dbj_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcds-dbj-22">[22]</a></sup> Until December 2003, it owned <a href="/wiki/Donatos_Pizza" title="Donatos Pizza">Donatos Pizza</a>, and it owned a small share of <a href="/wiki/Aroma_Caf%C3%A9" title="Aroma Café">Aroma Café</a> from 1999 to 2001. On August 27, 2007, McDonald's sold <a href="/wiki/Boston_Market" title="Boston Market">Boston Market</a> to <a href="/wiki/Sun_Capital_Partners" title="Sun Capital Partners">Sun Capital Partners</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p><p>Notably, McDonald's has increased shareholder dividends for 25 consecutive years,<sup id="cite_ref-ReutersOnMcDividend_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersOnMcDividend-24">[24]</a></sup> making it one of the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500_Dividend_Aristocrats" title="S&amp;P 500 Dividend Aristocrats">S&amp;P 500 Dividend Aristocrats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-investopediaDivAristocrat_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-investopediaDivAristocrat-25">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-seekAlphaFullListDivArist_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seekAlphaFullListDivArist-26">[26]</a></sup> The company is ranked 131st on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> of the largest United States corporations by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In October 2012, its monthly sales fell for the first time in nine years.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In 2014, its quarterly sales fell for the first time in seventeen years, when its sales dropped for the entirety of 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p><p>In the United States, it is reported that drive-throughs account for 70 percent of sales.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> McDonald's closed down 184 restaurants in the United States in 2015, which was 59 more than what they planned to open.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cutstores_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cutstores-33">[33]</a></sup> This move was the first time McDonald's had a net decrease in the number of locations in the United States since 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-cutstores_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cutstores-33">[33]</a></sup></p><p>The McDonalds on-demand delivery concept, which began in 2017 with a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Uber_Eats" title="Uber Eats">Uber Eats</a> and added <a href="/wiki/DoorDash" title="DoorDash">DoorDash</a> in 2019, accounts for up to 3% of all business as of 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span></h3>
<p>For the fiscal year 2018, McDonalds reported earnings of US$5.9 billion, with an annual revenue of US$21.0 billion, a decrease of 7.9% over the previous fiscal cycle. McDonald's shares traded at over $145 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over US$134.5 billion in September 2018.
</p>

</td>
<td>210,000
</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_model">Business model</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ray_kroc_1976.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ray_kroc_1976.jpg/150px-Ray_kroc_1976.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="182" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="719" data-file-height="871"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 150px;height: 182px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ray_kroc_1976.jpg/150px-Ray_kroc_1976.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="150" data-height="182" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ray_kroc_1976.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ray_Kroc" title="Ray Kroc">Ray Kroc</a> joined the chain in 1954 and built it into a global franchise, making it the most successful fast food corporation in the world</div></div></div>
<p>The company owns all the land on which its restaurants are situated, which is valued at an estimated $16 to $18 billion.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Seems implausible given how many restaurants are located within shopping centres (February 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The company earns a significant portion of its revenue from rental payments from franchisees. These rent payments rose 26 percent between 2010 and 2015, accounting for one-fifth of the company's total revenue at the end of the period.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In recent times, there have been calls to spin off the company's U.S. holdings into a potential <a href="/wiki/Real_estate_investment_trust" title="Real estate investment trust">real estate investment trust</a>, but the company announced at its investor conference on November 10, 2015, that this would not happen. CEO Steve Easterbrook discussed that pursuing the REIT option would pose too large a risk to the company's business model.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>The United Kingdom and Ireland business model is different from the U.S, in that fewer than 30 percent of restaurants are franchised, with the majority under the ownership of the company. McDonald's trains its franchisees and management at <a href="/wiki/Hamburger_University" title="Hamburger University">Hamburger University</a> located at its Chicago headquarters.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In other countries, McDonald's restaurants are operated by joint ventures of McDonald's Corporation and other, local entities or governments.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p><p>According to <i><a href="/wiki/Fast_Food_Nation" title="Fast Food Nation">Fast Food Nation</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Schlosser" title="Eric Schlosser">Eric Schlosser</a> (2001), nearly one in eight workers in the U.S. have at some time been employed by McDonald's. Employees are encouraged by McDonald's Corp. to maintain their health by singing along to their favorite songs in order to relieve stress, attending <a href="/wiki/Church_service" title="Church service">church services</a> in order to have a lower <a href="/wiki/Blood_pressure" title="Blood pressure">blood pressure</a>, and taking two vacations annually in order to reduce risk for <a href="/wiki/Myocardial_infarction" title="Myocardial infarction">myocardial infarction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> <i>Fast Food Nation</i> states that McDonald's is the largest private operator of playgrounds in the U.S., as well as the single largest purchaser of beef, pork, potatoes, and apples. The selection of meats McDonald's uses varies to some extent based on the culture of the host country.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span></h3>
<p>On June 13, 2016, McDonald's confirmed plans to move its global headquarters to <a href="/wiki/Chicago%27s_West_Loop" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago's West Loop">Chicago's West Loop</a> neighborhood in the <a href="/wiki/Near_West_Side,_Chicago" title="Near West Side, Chicago">Near West Side</a>. The 608,000-square-foot structure was built on the former site of <a href="/wiki/Harpo_Productions" title="Harpo Productions">Harpo Productions</a> (where the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Oprah_Winfrey_Show" title="The Oprah Winfrey Show">Show</a></i> and several other Harpo productions taped) and opened on June 4, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-west_side_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-west_side-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-move_HQ_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-move_HQ-6">[6]</a></sup></p><p>The McDonald's former headquarters complex, McDonald's Plaza, is located in <a href="/wiki/Oak_Brook,_Illinois" title="Oak Brook, Illinois">Oak Brook, Illinois</a>. It sits on the site of the former headquarters and stabling area of Paul Butler, the founder of Oak Brook.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> McDonald's moved into the Oak Brook facility from an office within the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Loop" title="Chicago Loop">Chicago Loop</a> in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_directors">Board of directors</span></h3>
<p>As of January 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=McDonald%27s&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the board of directors had the following members:<sup id="cite_ref-Board_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Board-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Enrique_Hernandez_Jr." title="Enrique Hernandez Jr.">Enrique Hernandez Jr.</a>, non-executive chairman; president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Inter-Con_Security" title="Inter-Con Security">Inter-Con Security</a></li>
<li>Lloyd H. Dean, president and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Dignity_Health" title="Dignity Health">Dignity Health</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Steve_Easterbrook" title="Steve Easterbrook">Stephen J. Easterbrook</a>, president and CEO of McDonald's</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_A._Eckert" title="Robert A. Eckert">Robert A. Eckert</a>, operating partner of <a href="/wiki/Friedman_Fleischer_%26_Lowe" title="Friedman Fleischer &amp; Lowe">Friedman Fleischer &amp; Lowe</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Margo_Georgiadis" title="Margo Georgiadis">Margo Georgiadis</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Ancestry.com" title="Ancestry.com">Ancestry.com</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jeanne_P._Jackson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jeanne P. Jackson (page does not exist)">Jeanne P. Jackson</a>, CEO of MSP Capital</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Richard_H._Lenny&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Richard H. Lenny (page does not exist)">Richard H. Lenny</a>, non-executive of <a href="/wiki/Conagra_Brands" title="Conagra Brands">Conagra Brands</a></li>
<li>John J. Mulligan, executive vice president and COO of <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target Corporation</a></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sheila_A._Penrose&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sheila A. Penrose (page does not exist)">Sheila A. Penrose</a>, non-executive chairman of <a href="/wiki/Jones_Lang_LaSalle" class="mw-redirect" title="Jones Lang LaSalle">Jones Lang LaSalle</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_W._Rogers_Jr." title="John W. Rogers Jr.">John W. Rogers Jr.</a>, chairman and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Investments" title="Ariel Investments">Ariel Investments</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Miles_D._White" title="Miles D. White">Miles D. White</a>, chairman and CEO of <a href="/wiki/Abbott_Laboratories" title="Abbott Laboratories">Abbott Laboratories</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andrew_J._McKenna" title="Andrew J. McKenna">Andrew J. McKenna</a>, chairman emeritus. Also chairman emeritus of Schwarz Supply Source</li></ul><p>On March 1, 2015, after being chief brand officer of McDonald's and its former head in the UK and northern Europe, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Easterbrook" title="Steve Easterbrook">Steve Easterbrook</a> became CEO, succeeding Don Thompson, who stepped down on January 28, 2015.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_operations">Global operations</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_with_McDonald%27s_restaurants" title="List of countries with McDonald's restaurants">List of countries with McDonald's restaurants</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_availability_of_McDonald%27s_products" title="International availability of McDonald's products">International availability of McDonald's products</a></div>
 <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg/300px-McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="151" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="848" data-file-height="427"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 300px;height: 151px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg/300px-McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="300" data-height="151" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg/450px-McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg/600px-McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McDonaldsWorldLocations.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries with McDonald's restaurants, showing their first year with its first restaurant</div></div></div>
<p>McDonald's has become emblematic of <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">globalization</a>, sometimes referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/McDonaldization" title="McDonaldization">McDonaldization</a>" of society. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> newspaper uses the "<a href="/wiki/Big_Mac_Index" title="Big Mac Index">Big Mac Index</a>": the comparison of the cost of a <a href="/wiki/Big_Mac" title="Big Mac">Big Mac</a> in various world <a href="/wiki/Currency" title="Currency">currencies</a> can be used to informally judge these currencies' <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>. Switzerland has the most expensive Big Mac in the world as of July 2015, while the country with the least expensive Big Mac is <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> (albeit for a <a href="/wiki/Maharaja_Mac" class="mw-redirect" title="Maharaja Mac">Maharaja Mac</a>—the next cheapest Big Mac is <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Friedman" title="Thomas Friedman">Thomas Friedman</a> said that no country with a McDonald's had gone to war with another;<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> however, the "<a href="/wiki/Golden_Arches_Theory_of_Conflict_Prevention" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Arches Theory of Conflict Prevention">Golden Arches Theory of Conflict Prevention</a>" is incorrect. Exceptions are the 1989 <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Panama" title="United States invasion of Panama">United States invasion of Panama</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_War#The_NATO_bombing_campaign" title="Kosovo War">NATO's bombing of Serbia in 1999</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2006_Lebanon_War" title="2006 Lebanon War">2006 Lebanon War</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_war" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 South Ossetia war">2008 South Ossetia war</a>. McDonald's suspended operations in its corporate-owned stores in Crimea after Russia annexed the region in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On August 20, 2014, as tensions between the United States and Russia strained over events in Ukraine, and the resultant U.S. sanctions, the Russian government temporarily shut down four McDonald's outlets in Moscow, citing sanitary concerns. The company has operated in Russia since 1990 and at August 2014 had 438 stores across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-McDonaldsMoscow_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McDonaldsMoscow-64">[64]</a></sup> On August 23, 2014, Russian Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Arkady_Dvorkovich" title="Arkady Dvorkovich">Arkady Dvorkovich</a> ruled out any government move to ban McDonald's and dismissed the notion that the temporary closures had anything to do with the sanctions.<sup id="cite_ref-McDonaldsRussia_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McDonaldsRussia-65">[65]</a></sup></p><p>Some observers have suggested that the company should be given credit for increasing the standard of service in markets that it enters. A group of anthropologists in a study entitled <i>Golden Arches East</i><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> looked at the impact McDonald's had on <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asia</a> and Hong Kong, in particular. When it opened in Hong Kong in 1975, McDonald's was the first restaurant to consistently offer clean restrooms, driving customers to demand the same of other restaurants and institutions. McDonald's has taken to partnering up with <a href="/wiki/Sinopec" title="Sinopec">Sinopec</a>, the second largest oil company in the People's Republic of China, as it takes advantage of the country's growing use of personal vehicles by opening numerous drive-thru restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> McDonald's has opened a McDonald's restaurant and McCafé on the underground premises of the French <a href="/wiki/Fine_art" title="Fine art">fine arts</a> museum, <a href="/wiki/The_Louvre" class="mw-redirect" title="The Louvre">The Louvre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p><p>The company stated it would open vegetarian-only restaurants in India by mid-2013.<sup id="cite_ref-wsj20120905_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj20120905-69">[69]</a></sup></p><p>On January 9, 2017, 80% of the franchise rights in the mainland China and in Hong Kong were sold for US$2.08 billion to a consortium of <a href="/wiki/CITIC_Limited" title="CITIC Limited">CITIC Limited</a> (for 32%) and private equity funds managed by CITIC Capital (for 20%) and <a href="/wiki/The_Carlyle_Group" title="The Carlyle Group">Carlyle</a> (for 20%), which CITIC Limited and CITIC Capital would formed a joint venture to own the stake.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
